  "body": "549 cases were found by faultfinder for the headwords of PUI ( Purana Index)\r\n\r\nThese comprise headwords of  PUI that\r\n\r\n* occur only in PUI\r\n* have spelling patterns that \r\n  * don't occur among the MW headwords (as detected from faultfinder),\r\n  * are not of the 'rxx' variety.\r\n\r\nI've put pui-fuzzyalpha.txt [here](https://github.com/sanskrit-lexicon/CORRECTIONS/blob/master/dictionaries/PUI/pui-fuzzyalpha.txt)  and pui-fuzzalpha.html [here](https://github.com/sanskrit-lexicon/CORRECTIONS/blob/master/dictionaries/PUI/pui-fuzzyalpha.html), \r\nand as active html page [here](http://funderburkjim.github.io/fuzzywork/pui-fuzzyalpha.html).\r\n\r\nThe instructions are as per [issue 100](https://github.com/sanskrit-lexicon/CORRECTIONS/issues/100).\r\n\r\n\r\n",

    "body": "A note before I proceed with this issue.\r\n\r\nThis dictionary is notorious for misspelling 'M' for 'm' even if it is mandatory to have 'M'.\r\ne.g. \r\n```\r\n008 anuvamSa\r\n015 arkavamSa\r\n020 azwAvimSatitamamanu\r\n```\r\n\r\nSimilarly it uses 'm' instead of paJcama varga letters (which is not at all tolerable).\r\n'M' would have been OK, but 'm' is gross.\r\ne.g.\r\n```\r\n014 arizwasamjYa\r\n016 arkasamkrama\r\n017 alamkAras\r\n```\r\n\r\nI would be correcting both types to 'M'."

    "created_at": "2015-04-21T22:26:28Z",
    "updated_at": "2015-04-21T22:26:28Z",
    "body": "@Shalu411 Here's an explanation for the specific case. 001\r\n\r\nJust look at the line with the arrow: `001 akzayawrtIyA ->  (akzayatftIyA)`\r\n\r\nThe word up for correction is the word to the left of the arrow:  `akzayawrtIyA `\r\n\r\nThe word (or words) to the right of the arrow are suggestions as to what the correct spelling *might* be.  \r\n\r\nYou would look at the scanned image using  the active html page [here](http://funderburkjim.github.io/fuzzywork/pui-fuzzyalpha.html):\r\n![image](https://cloud.githubusercontent.com/assets/6393033/7263836/05861376-e853-11e4-9ad9-42268affb519.png)\r\nwhich leads you to\r\n![image](https://cloud.githubusercontent.com/assets/6393033/7263860/2c730890-e853-11e4-9d7e-bf89c2026bf6.png)\r\n\r\n\r\nIn this case, even though the text has retroflect 't', that is clearly wrong (we could say its a print error or\r\na scan error).   In this instance, we agree with the suggestion .  So , in your local copy of pui-fuzzyalpha.txt\r\nyou would change that line with the arrow from\r\n\r\n```\r\n001 akzayawrtIyA ->  (akzayatftIyA)\r\n```\r\nto\r\n```\r\n001 akzayawrtIyA -> akzayatftIyA :  (akzayatftIyA)\r\n```\r\nI.e., the corrected spelling goes to the right of the arrow AND  a 'Colon' follows the correction, to separate it\r\n  from suggestions.\r\n\r\nThat's it.\r\n\r\nSince Dhaval is working on PUI,  you don't need to.  But the same principles apply to PGN in issue 103,\r\nwhich I hope you will try.\r\n\r\nHope this helps some.\r\n"

Programmatically, hw1.py would probably be the function that\r\nshould make the distinction.\r\n\r\nThus we are not 'correcting' pui.txt  but rather we are enhancing the 'key1' metadata, which ultimately appears in puihw2.txt and fills the role of 'key1' in pui.xml. (and is used as the 'citation' form in headword\r\nlookups for PUI).\r\n\r\nIt might be that in the corrections file you are dealing with, you should leave this as NO CHANGE.\r\nAnd that a separate list of 'plurals' should be developed for PUI (pui_plurals.txt)  and this list would be\r\nadded as an input to hw1.py for pui.\r\n\r\nHow does this approach sound to you?\r\n"

There were a few where I had questions.\r\n\r\nFirst group,  'L' (SLP1).\r\n* cUxikas -> cULikas    (AS coding is Cu1l2ikas)\r\n  * I think this is plural (plurality will be dealt with separately in another issue, as mentioned above)\r\n  * MW has 'cUlika'\r\n* vinDyamOxIyas -> vinDyamOLIyas  (AS coding is Vindhyamaul2i1yas)\r\n  * Also a plural\r\n  * MW has vinDyamOleya\r\n\r\nThe letter in question: IAST  l with under-dot == AS l2  ==? SLP1 L.\r\n\r\nMW shows both these examples with the semivowel 'l'.\r\n\r\nThe L occurs in MW in word 'iLas' =   and in Roman (IAST) display = ias\r\n\r\nBut also, SLP1 kxp displays as 'kp' in MW =  and the 'x' represents vowel\r\n\r\nIn [IAST](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Alphabet_of_Sanskrit_Transliteration)  there is no\r\nmention of   (l with dot below).\r\n\r\nAlso,  is not part of the Sanskrit alphabet as I learned it, although  it appears in this [alphabet](http://www.omniglot.com/writing/sanskrit.htm).\r\n\r\nSo, there are several confusions about   that I need to get straight before entering these changes.\r\n* How does one pronounce  ?\r\n* Is  really part of Sanskrit alphabet? If so, does the standard IAST representation of SLP1 'x' differ?"

    "body": "garutmaTfdayA -> garutmathfdayA\r\n\r\nGarutmathr2daya1 = AS\r\n\r\nThis is interesting, as it shows an ambiguity in the IAST :  we are interpreting the 'th' separately  (the 't'\r\nends Garutmat, and the 'h' begins hr2daya1), whereas 'usually' 'th' means the aspirated hard dental.\r\n\r\nSince this change does not represent an error in the digitization, but rather a special handling required in the\r\ngeneration of SLP1 from IAST, it will need to be handled in hw2.py.\r\n\r\n(This is not a question, but a comment.)\r\n"

    "body": "1. `How does one pronounce  ?`\r\nAs  is instead of , same is the pronunciation (and h instead of h). Pali grammarians (p. 40, Pali Language 1965) note that pronunciation of  gets mixed with  sometimes. In IAST a mix happens.\r\n\r\n2. `Is  really part of Sanskrit alphabet? If so, why is it absent from so many listings of the alphabet.`\r\nThere is no such thing as Sanskrit alphabet, it's a fiction. For the need of Vedic texts and Marathi  is used. Sanskrit is a language. Devanagari is a writing syllabary. It's one of the alphabets widely used nowadays, similar to Bengali characters used just 200 years ago.\r\n\r\n3. `If so is the above omniglot display correct in its placement in alphabet?`\r\nYes and no. Omniglot's creator thinks I'm an authority (see http://www.omniglot.com/blog/?p=682 and http://www.omniglot.com/blog/?p=621) and I as an authority can say that it is positioned there only because there was some free place, no scientific background. It should be in a footnote.\r\n\r\n4. `Is there a 'standard' IAST representation? If so, does the standard IAST representation of SLP1 'x' differ?`\r\nSee p. 12 of http://shashir.autodidactus.org/shashir_umich/dl/rapportdetranscription.pdf - IAST always had only , but the mixing was always there (see a whole paragraph on it). I hardly understand how it can differ from SLP1 even theoretically, because SLP1 is a pure abstraction that has nothing to do with phonetics, diacritics of tradition."
